      <p>
       <b>
        Fang
       </b>
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'f' in 'find'">
            f
           </span>
           <span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">
            ɒ
           </span>
           <span title="/ŋ/: 'ng' in 'sing'">
            ŋ
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       is a Central African language spoken by around 1 million people in Cameroon, Gabon, Equatorial Guinea, São Tomé and Príncipe, and the Congo Republic. It is the dominant
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bantu_language" title="Bantu language">
        Bantu language
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">
        Gabon
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">
        Equatorial Guinea
       </a>
       . It is related to the
       <a href="/wiki/Bulu_language" title="Bulu language">
        Bulu
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ewondo_language" title="Ewondo language">
        Ewondo
       </a>
       languages of southern
       <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">
        Cameroon
       </a>
       . Fang is spoken in northern Gabon, southern Cameroon, throughout Equatorial Guinea, in the Republic of the Congo, and small fractions of the islands of São Tomé and Príncipe. Under President
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Mac%C3%ADas_Nguema" title="Francisco Macías Nguema">
        Macías Nguema
       </a>
       , Fang was the official language of Equatorial Guinea.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are many different variants of Fang in Gabon and Cameroon. Maho (2009) lists Southwest Fang as a distinct language. The other dialects are Ntoumou, Okak, Mekê, Atsi (Batsi), Nzaman (Zaman), Mveni, and Mvaïe.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Corpus_and_lexicology">
        Corpus and lexicology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fang_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Corpus and lexicology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Despite lacking any truly certain corpus of Fang's literary body, it is of note that linguists have, in the past, made attempts to compile dictionaries and lexicons for the Fang language. The two most notable ones to be either proposed or fully compiled were made by Maillard (2007)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and Bibang (2014). Neither created a direct Fang-English dictionary, but opted instead to separate the two languages via a third European language as a bridge for various loanwords.
      </p>
      <p>
       The translation efforts to English have been done through Romance languages: specifically, Spanish and French. The latter of the two languages would likely have had the most impact on the language, given the occupation of Gabon by the French during the existence of French Equatorial Africa (itself part of French West Africa), which lasted 75 years from 1885 to 1960. To a lesser extent, in São Tomé and Príncipe, Portuguese also likely has influenced the dialects of Fang present there, due to the country being occupied by Portugal for most of the islands' history of habitation.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span id="Phonology.5B5.5D">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology[5]">
        Phonology
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-5">
          [5]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fang_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Phonology[5]">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">
        Vowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fang_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Vowels">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Fang has 7 vowels, each of which can have short or long realizations.
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">
       <caption>
        Vowel Phonemes
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">
          Front
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Vowel_length" title="Vowel length">
          short/long
         </a>
         )
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Back_vowel" title="Back vowel">
          Back
         </a>
         (short/long)
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Close_vowel" title="Close vowel">
          Close
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          i iː
         </span>
         (ĩ)
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          u uː
         </span>
         (ũ)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_vowel" title="Close-mid vowel">
          Close-mid
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          e eː
         </span>
         (ẽ)
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          o oː
         </span>
         (õ)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_vowel" title="Open-mid vowel">
          Open-mid
         </a>
        </th>
        <td style="font-size:larger;">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ɛ ɛː
         </span>
         (ɛ̃)
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ɔ ɔː
         </span>
         (ɔ̃)
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Open_vowel" title="Open vowel">
          Open
         </a>
        </th>
        <td colspan="2">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          a aː
         </span>
         (ã)
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Nasal_vowel" title="Nasal vowel">
        Nasal vowels
       </a>
       are allophones of the respective oral vowels, when followed by a nasal consonant
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ŋ]
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɲ]
       </span>
       . Words can not start with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɛ]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [i]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɔ]
       </span>
       nor
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [u]
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diphthongs">
        Diphthongs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fang_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Diphthongs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Diphthongs can be a combination of any vowel with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [j]
       </span>
       or
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [w]
       </span>
       , as well as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ea]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [oe]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [oa]
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ua]
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tone">
        Tone
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fang_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tone">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Fang distinguishes between 4 different tones, conventionally called: high, low, rising and falling. The former two are simple tones, while the latter are compound tones. One vowel in a sequences of vowels can be elided in casual speech, though its tone remains and attaches to the remaining vowel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">
        Consonants
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fang_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Consonants">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In Fang, there are 24 consonants. The majority of them can become
       <a href="/wiki/Prenasalized_consonant" title="Prenasalized consonant">
        prenasalized
       </a>
       :
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
       <caption>
        Consonant phonemes
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Labial_consonant" title="Labial consonant">
          Labial
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
          Dental
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
          Alveolar
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveopalatal_consonant" title="Alveopalatal consonant">
          Alveopalatal
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">
          Velar
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Glottal_consonant" title="Glottal consonant">
          Glottal
         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Nasal_consonant" title="Nasal consonant">
          Nasal
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          m
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          n
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ɲ
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ŋ
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Stop_consonant" title="Stop consonant">
          Stop
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          p b
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          mp mb
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          t d
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          nt nd
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          k ɡ
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ŋk ŋg
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          k͡p ɡ͡b
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ŋk͡p ŋɡ͡b
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ʔ
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Affricate_consonant" title="Affricate consonant">
          Affricate
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          t͡s d͡z
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          nt͡s nd͡z
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Fricative_consonant" title="Fricative consonant">
          Fricative
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          f v
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ɱf ɱv
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          s z
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ns nz
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          h
         </span>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <th align="left">
         <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">
          Approximant
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          l
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          j
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ɲj
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          w
         </span>
         <br/>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          nw
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr align="center">
        <th align="left">
         <a href="/wiki/Flap_consonant" title="Flap consonant">
          Tap
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          ɾ
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <br/>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /h/
       </span>
       is only used in interjections and loanwords. Words can not start with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ŋ/
       </span>
       , except when followed by a velar consonant.
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɾ/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /z/
       </span>
       also are restricted from word-initial position.
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /g/
       </span>
       and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /p/
       </span>
       can only come in word-initial position in words of foreign origin, although in many of these cases,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /g/
       </span>
       becomes realized as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ŋg]
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The morpheme "gh" is pronounced as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɾ
       </span>
       in the case of the word "Beyoghe" (the Fang term for Libreville); one of several changes to pronunciation by morphology.
      </p>
      <p>
       It is also important to note that in Fang, at every "hiatus" (shock of two vowels), such as in "Ma adzi", it is required for one to make the second word an aphetism, dropping the pronunciation of the
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        aː
       </span>
       sound at the start of the second word (e.g. "Ma dzi") in order to make grammatically correct sentences.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phrases">
        Phrases
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fang_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Phrases">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Although the Fang language does not have an official orthography, native speakers happen to use the extended Latin alphabet with specific accents. Due to the enormous geographic region it covers, and the large amount of Fang dialects, the following list may not be entirely accurate; one issue of note is the lack of marking for tones. Regardless, common phrases for the
       <a href="/wiki/Oyem" title="Oyem">
        Oyem
       </a>
       area of northern Gabon include:
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         English
        </th>
        <th>
         Fang
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Hello (to one person)
        </td>
        <td>
         M'bolo/Mbolo
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Hello (to several people)
        </td>
        <td>
         M'bolani/Mbolo'ani
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Hello (response)
        </td>
        <td>
         Am'bolo; Am'bolani
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         How are you?
        </td>
        <td>
         Y'o num vah?
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         response
        </td>
        <td>
         M'a num vah
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Where are you going
        </td>
        <td>
         Wa kuh vay?; Wa ke vé?
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I'm going home
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma kuh Andah
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Are you okay?
        </td>
        <td>
         Onevoghe?
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I'm going to school
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma ke see-kolo
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I'm going for a walk
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma ke ma woolou
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I'm hungry
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="fan" xml:lang="fan">
           Ma woh zeng
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I'm sick
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma kwan
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I understand French
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma wok Flacci
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I don't understand Fang
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma wok ki Fang
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I don't speak Fang
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma kobe ki Fang
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         What did you say
        </td>
        <td>
         Wa dzon ah dzeh?
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I said...
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma dzon ah...
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Holy_cow_(expression)" title="Holy cow (expression)">
          Holy cow
         </a>
         !
        </td>
        <td>
         A tara dzam!
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         I want to eat
        </td>
        <td>
         Ma cuma adji/adzi
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Thank you
        </td>
        <td>
         Akiba
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Thank you very much
        </td>
        <td>
         Abora
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
